THIS Index to Volumes I.-XVI. of the Annual was undertaken in connexion with the celebration of the Twenty-fifth Anniversary of the Foundation of the British School at Athens. As its main purpose is to make more accessible the contents of the Reports of the Excavations undertaken by the School, or in connexion with it, especially those at Knossos, Palaikastro, and Sparta, these have been indexed in considerable detail, pending a fuller publication in book-form. But for several of the longer or more important among the other articles, e.g. Lycosura, Rhitsona, it seemed advisable to make a short pre'cis under one heading, rather than to multiply miscellaneous references. Hence some of the general entries, e.g. Pottery, or Sculpture, may seem at first sight disproportionately short, in comparison with e.g. those under geographical headings. In the transliteration of proper names I have followed, as far as possible, the guidance of the more recent volumes of the Annual. I have not, however, aimed at complete consistency, but have merely tried to make uniform in every case the various spellings of any given word, employed by each contributor. I wish to acknowledge here the ready assistance of many friends, especially of Miss C. A. Hutton, who, besides undertaking the writing of the bulk of the slips for Volumes I.-V., has most materially lightened for me the task of seeing the work through the Press, and has given me the benefit of her experience on countless points. Mr. M. N. Tod most kindly read the</page><page sequence="6">vi PREFACE. proof-sheets of the Epigraphical Index, enabling me to eliminate many unnoticed inaccuracies. Professor R. C. Bosanquet, Mr. J. P. Droop, and Mr. F. W. Hasluck have helped me with expert advice on various points of detail. But for all faults, whether in arrangement, or actual errors, or omissions, I alone am responsible. I should like also to record my indebtedness to the Committee of the School for entrusting to me the compilation of this Index, and to the Secretary, Mr. J. ff. Baker-Penoyre, for every facility given me during its preparation. I hope nothing more for -it than that, in spite of the short- comings of which I am only too conscious, it will prove of real assistance to Archaeologists. A. M. WOODWARD. LIVERPOOL, January, 1912.</page><page sequence="7">INDEX OF AUTHORS B</page><page sequence="8">INDEX OF AUTHORS. ANDERSON, J. G. C. An Epigraphic Miscellany. III. Io6. The following words or abbreviations are inserted after the number of the page to which reference is made, to denote inscriptions engraved on some unusual material: Br. (= Brick), Bronze, Gem, Ivory, Tc. (=Terracotta), T. (=Tile), V. (=Vase). Christian Inscriptions (Epitaphs, Inscriptions from Byzantine Churches of all dates, etc.) are denoted by (Chr.). Inscriptions on coins are omitted. In the use of brackets, etc., the usual epigraphical conventions have been followed.</page><page sequence="16">GREEK. I.-PROPER NAMES. 'A, xiv. 256 (V.), 281 (V.) All Finds from Excavations published in detail in the Annual, are indexed under the name of the site excavated, not under the class of object found, e.g. : all pottery found at Knossos, Palaikastro, and Sparta is indexed under those headings, not under' Pottery.' Cross-references are given in all the more important instances, e.g. : Pottery, Laconian, 'see Sparta, s.v. Pottery.' Excavation-records are indexed under subject-headings :-I. Topography (Sites, Buildings, etc.). II. Finds. III. Civilization (Human Figures, Life, Religion, etc.). To economise space, the Finds at Sparta are further sub-divided into A, 'Finds from the Whole Area,' and B, 'Finds from the Separate Sites.'
